bg: bg [job_spec ...]
    Move jobs to the background.
    
    Place the jobs identified by each JOB_SPEC in the background, as if they
    had been started with `&'.  If JOB_SPEC is not present, the shell's notion
    of the current job is used.
    
    Exit Status:
    Returns success unless job control is not enabled or an error occurs.

[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       ls - list directory contents[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mls[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       List information about the FILEs (the current directory by default).  Sort entries alphabetically if none of[m
       [1m-cftuvSUX[0m nor [1m--sort[0m is specified.[m
[m
       Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.[m
[m
       [1m-a[0m, [1m--all[0m[m
              do not ignore entries starting with .[m
[m
       [1m-A[0m, [1m--almost-all[0m[m
              do not list implied . and ..[m
[m
       [1m--author[0m[m
              with [1m-l[0m, print the author of each file[m
[m
       [1m-b[0m, [1m--escape[0m[m
              print C-style escapes for nongraphic characters[m
[m
       [1m--block-size[0m=[4mSIZE[24m[m
              scale sizes by SIZE before printing them; e.g., '--block-size=M' prints sizes in units  of  1,048,576[m
              bytes; see SIZE format below[m
[m
       [1m-B[0m, [1m--ignore-backups[0m[m
              do not list implied entries ending with ~[m

]0;litepoint@litepoint-Latitude-E6440: ~/Desktop/Shell_script[01;32mlitepoint@litepoint-Latitude-E6440[00m:[01;34m~/Desktop/Shell_script[00m$ cat /etc/profile
# /etc/profile: system-wide .profile file for the Bourne shell (sh(1))
# and Bourne compatible shells (bash(1), ksh(1), ash(1), ...).

if [ "${PS1-}" ]; then
  if [ "${BASH-}" ] && [ "$BASH" != "/bin/sh" ]; then
    # The file bash.bashrc already sets the default PS1.
    # PS1='\h:\w\$ '
    if [ -f /etc/bash.bashrc ]; then
      . /etc/bash.bashrc
    fi
  else
    if [ "`id -u`" -eq 0 ]; then
      PS1='# '
    else
      PS1='$ '
    fi
  fi
fi

if [ -d /etc/profile.d ]; then
  for i in /etc/profile.d/*.sh; do
    if [ -r $i ]; then
      . $i
    fi
  done
  unset i
fi

[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=SIGNAL(7)                                    Linux Programmer's Manual                                    SIGNAL(7)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       signal - overview of signals[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Linux supports both POSIX reliable signals (hereinafter "standard signals") and POSIX real-time signals.[m
[m
   [1mSignal[0m [1mdispositions[0m[m
       Each  signal  has  a  current [4mdisposition[24m, which determines how the process behaves when it is delivered the[m
       signal.[m
[m
       The entries in the "Action" column of the tables below specify the default disposition for each  signal,  as[m
       follows:[m
[m
       Term   Default action is to terminate the process.[m
[m
       Ign    Default action is to ignore the signal.[m
[m
       Core   Default action is to terminate the process and dump core (see [1mcore[0m(5)).[m
[m
       Stop   Default action is to stop the process.[m
[m
       Cont   Default action is to continue the process if it is currently stopped.[m
[m
       A  process can change the disposition of a signal using [1msigaction[0m(2) or [1msignal[0m(2).  (The latter is less por‐[m
       table when establishing a signal handler; see [1msignal[0m(2) for details.)  Using these system calls,  a  process[m
       can  elect  one  of  the following behaviors to occur on delivery of the signal: perform the default action;[m
       ignore the signal; or catch the signal with a [4msignal[24m [4mhandler[24m, a programmer-defined function that is automat‐[m
       ically  invoked  when  the  signal  is  delivered.  (By default, the signal handler is invoked on the normal[m
       process stack.  It is possible to arrange that the signal handler  uses  an  alternate  stack;  see  [1msigalt‐[0m[m
       [1mstack[0m(2) for a discussion of how to do this and when it might be useful.)[m
[m
       The signal disposition is a per-process attribute: in a multithreaded application, the disposition of a par‐[m
